<analysis>**original_problem_statement:**
L'utilisateur a initialement demandé un calculateur d'empreinte carbone, qui a évolué vers une application complète. Les demandes récentes de l'utilisateur se sont concentrées sur des améliorations majeures et des refactorisations :
1.  **Harmonisation du Design**: Aligner le design de toute l'application (cartes, ombres, modaux) sur le style de l'onglet Résultats.
2.  **Amélioration du Graphique de Trajectoire**: Le rendre plus lisible et aligné avec les autres graphiques, avec une meilleure visualisation des scénarios.
3.  **Robustesse de la Gestion des Scénarios**: Transformer les scénarios (qui étaient basés sur du texte libre) en entités propres dans la base de données pour éviter les erreurs de saisie et permettre un affichage multi-périodes.
4.  **Correction de Bug Préventive**: Suite à un rapport d'analyse externe (qui s'est avéré incorrect pour le code actuel), l'agent a appliqué une correction préventive pour rendre les données d'activité plus robustes en normalisant le  au moment de l'écriture.
5.  **Refactoring Technique**: Découper le composant monolithique  pour améliorer la maintenabilité.
6.  **Migration de la Base de Données**: Remplacer la base de données des facteurs d'émission par une nouvelle version (BAFU 2025), une tâche majeure en cours.

**PRODUCT REQUIREMENTS:**
*   **TÂCHE UI — Harmonisation du Design**: Appliquer le style visuel de l'onglet Résultats à l'ensemble de l'application. (Terminé)
*   **TÂCHE UX — Amélioration du Graphique Trajectoire**: Refondre le graphique pour utiliser des barres empilées, des couleurs cohérentes et une meilleure visualisation des scénarios. (Terminé)
*   **TÂCHE ARCHITECTURE — Robustesse des Scénarios**: Migrer les scénarios vers une collection dédiée et mettre à jour la logique pour les gérer comme des entités. (Terminé)
*   **TÂCHE REFACTORING — ProductWizard.js**: Découper le composant en plusieurs sous-composants et un hook de logique. (Terminé)
*   **TÂCHE MIGRATION — Base de Données des Facteurs d'Émission**: Intégrer la nouvelle base de données BAFU 2025. (En cours)

**User's preferred language**: Français

**what currently exists?**
Une application full-stack (React/FastAPI/MongoDB) dont les fonctionnalités et le design ont été significativement améliorés.
-   **Design Cohérent**: L'ensemble de l'application, y compris les cartes de contenu et les modaux, suit un style visuel unifié (, ,  pour les modaux).
-   **Graphique de Trajectoire Avancé**: A été entièrement refactorisé pour afficher les données réelles en barres empilées (Scope 1, 2, 3) avec des couleurs cohérentes, la trajectoire cible en fond, et les scénarios en barres fantômes transparentes. L'affichage multi-périodes pour un même scénario est fonctionnel.
-   **Gestion de Scénarios Robuste**: Les scénarios sont désormais des entités propres dans une collection . La création de nouveaux exercices est liée à ces entités via un , avec un dropdown de sélection et une validation pour empêcher les doublons sur une même année.
-   **Code Robuste**: La normalisation des scopes ( -> /) se fait désormais à l'écriture des activités dans la base de données, et non plus seulement à la lecture, grâce à un service partagé .
-   **Composant  Refactorisé**: Le fichier monolithique de ~1000 lignes a été découpé en 7 sous-composants et un hook , améliorant drastiquement la lisibilité et la maintenabilité.
-   L'application est en cours de migration vers une nouvelle base de données de facteurs d'émission.

  - **Harmonisation complète du Design**: Toutes les pages (, , , , etc.) ont été mises à jour pour utiliser un style de carte cohérent ().
  - **Harmonisation des Modals**: Standardisation de tous les modaux de l'application pour utiliser une ombre  et un fond .
  - **Refonte du Graphique de Trajectoire**: Remplacé l'ancien graphique par des barres empilées pour les scopes, une zone unique pour la cible, et des barres fantômes pour les scénarios. L'espacement a été réduit pour une meilleure lisibilité.
- **Architecture & Refactoring**:
  - **Gestion de Scénarios Robuste**: Migration des scénarios de texte libre vers une collection  dédiée avec des références . Le flux de création a été mis à jour avec un dropdown et une validation anti-doublon. Le graphique affiche désormais toutes les périodes d'un scénario sélectionné.
  - **Refactoring de **: Le composant monolithique de 978 lignes a été découpé en 8 fichiers plus petits et gérables (1 orchestrateur, 1 hook, 5 étapes, 1 fichier de constantes).
  - **Normalisation des Scopes à l'écriture**: La logique de mappage des scopes a été centralisée dans  et est maintenant appelée lors de la création des activités, rendant les données en base plus fiables. Une migration a été effectuée sur les données existantes.

     - **Why to solve this issue and what will be achieved with this?** Réduire la charge sur la base de données et la latence réseau. C'est une bonne pratique de performance.

**Code Architecture**


**Key Technical Concepts**
- **Migration de Schéma et de Données (MongoDB & Python)**: Création d'une nouvelle collection , mise à jour des schémas existants pour utiliser des références (), et écriture de scripts pour migrer les données existantes.
- **Refactoring de Composants (React)**: Application du principe de responsabilité unique en découpant un composant monolithique en une structure plus maintenable (orchestrateur, hooks, composants de présentation).
- **Centralisation de la Logique Métier (Backend)**: Extraction d'une logique de normalisation dupliquée dans un service partagé pour garantir la cohérence (principe DRY).
- **Visualisation de Données Avancée (Recharts)**: Implémentation d'un graphique complexe combinant des barres empilées groupées, une , une , et une légende personnalisée pour un affichage multi-séries.

self = <PreparedRequest [POST]>, url = '/api/auth/login', params = OrderedDict()

    def prepare_url(self, url, params):
        """Prepares the given HTTP URL."""
        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238
        if isinstance(url, bytes):
            url = url.decode("utf8")
        else:
            url = str(url)
    
        # Remove leading whitespaces from url
        url = url.lstrip()
    
        # Don't do any URL preparation for non-HTTP schemes like `mailto`,
        # `data` etc to work around exceptions from `url_parse`, which
        # handles RFC 3986 only.
        if ":" in url and not url.lower().startswith("http"):
            self.url = url
            return
    
        # Support for unicode domain names and paths.
        try:
            scheme, auth, host, port, path, query, fragment = parse_url(url)
        except LocationParseError as e:
            raise InvalidURL(*e.args)
    
        if not scheme:
>           raise MissingSchema(
                f"Invalid URL {url!r}: No scheme supplied. "
                f"Perhaps you meant https://{url}?"
            )
E           requests.exceptions.MissingSchema: Invalid URL '/api/auth/login': No scheme supplied. Perhaps you meant https:///api/auth/login?

self = <PreparedRequest [POST]>, url = '/api/auth/register'
params = OrderedDict()

    def prepare_url(self, url, params):
        """Prepares the given HTTP URL."""
        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238
        if isinstance(url, bytes):
            url = url.decode("utf8")
        else:
            url = str(url)
    
        # Remove leading whitespaces from url
        url = url.lstrip()
    
        # Don't do any URL preparation for non-HTTP schemes like `mailto`,
        # `data` etc to work around exceptions from `url_parse`, which
        # handles RFC 3986 only.
        if ":" in url and not url.lower().startswith("http"):
            self.url = url
            return
    
        # Support for unicode domain names and paths.
        try:
            scheme, auth, host, port, path, query, fragment = parse_url(url)
        except LocationParseError as e:
            raise InvalidURL(*e.args)
    
        if not scheme:
>           raise MissingSchema(
                f"Invalid URL {url!r}: No scheme supplied. "
                f"Perhaps you meant https://{url}?"
            )
E           requests.exceptions.MissingSchema: Invalid URL '/api/auth/register': No scheme supplied. Perhaps you meant https:///api/auth/register?

self = <PreparedRequest [POST]>, url = 'None/api/auth/login'
params = OrderedDict()

    def prepare_url(self, url, params):
        """Prepares the given HTTP URL."""
        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238
        if isinstance(url, bytes):
            url = url.decode("utf8")
        else:
            url = str(url)
    
        # Remove leading whitespaces from url
        url = url.lstrip()
    
        # Don't do any URL preparation for non-HTTP schemes like `mailto`,
        # `data` etc to work around exceptions from `url_parse`, which
        # handles RFC 3986 only.
        if ":" in url and not url.lower().startswith("http"):
            self.url = url
            return
    
        # Support for unicode domain names and paths.
        try:
            scheme, auth, host, port, path, query, fragment = parse_url(url)
        except LocationParseError as e:
            raise InvalidURL(*e.args)
    
        if not scheme:
>           raise MissingSchema(
                f"Invalid URL {url!r}: No scheme supplied. "
                f"Perhaps you meant https://{url}?"
            )
E           requests.exceptions.MissingSchema: Invalid URL 'None/api/auth/login': No scheme supplied. Perhaps you meant https://None/api/auth/login?

self = <PreparedRequest [POST]>, url = '/api/auth/login', params = OrderedDict()

    def prepare_url(self, url, params):
        """Prepares the given HTTP URL."""
        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238
        if isinstance(url, bytes):
            url = url.decode("utf8")
        else:
            url = str(url)
    
        # Remove leading whitespaces from url
        url = url.lstrip()
    
        # Don't do any URL preparation for non-HTTP schemes like `mailto`,
        # `data` etc to work around exceptions from `url_parse`, which
        # handles RFC 3986 only.
        if ":" in url and not url.lower().startswith("http"):
            self.url = url
            return
    
        # Support for unicode domain names and paths.
        try:
            scheme, auth, host, port, path, query, fragment = parse_url(url)
        except LocationParseError as e:
            raise InvalidURL(*e.args)
    
        if not scheme:
>           raise MissingSchema(
                f"Invalid URL {url!r}: No scheme supplied. "
                f"Perhaps you meant https://{url}?"
            )
E           requests.exceptions.MissingSchema: Invalid URL '/api/auth/login': No scheme supplied. Perhaps you meant https:///api/auth/login?

self = <PreparedRequest [POST]>, url = '/api/auth/login', params = OrderedDict()

    def prepare_url(self, url, params):
        """Prepares the given HTTP URL."""
        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238
        if isinstance(url, bytes):
            url = url.decode("utf8")
        else:
            url = str(url)
    
        # Remove leading whitespaces from url
        url = url.lstrip()
    
        # Don't do any URL preparation for non-HTTP schemes like `mailto`,
        # `data` etc to work around exceptions from `url_parse`, which
        # handles RFC 3986 only.
        if ":" in url and not url.lower().startswith("http"):
            self.url = url
            return
    
        # Support for unicode domain names and paths.
        try:
            scheme, auth, host, port, path, query, fragment = parse_url(url)
        except LocationParseError as e:
            raise InvalidURL(*e.args)
    
        if not scheme:

self = <PreparedRequest [POST]>, url = '/api/auth/login', params = OrderedDict()

    def prepare_url(self, url, params):
        """Prepares the given HTTP URL."""
        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238
        if isinstance(url, bytes):
            url = url.decode("utf8")
        else:
            url = str(url)
    
        # Remove leading whitespaces from url
        url = url.lstrip()
    
        # Don't do any URL preparation for non-HTTP schemes like `mailto`,
        # `data` etc to work around exceptions from `url_parse`, which
        # handles RFC 3986 only.
        if ":" in url and not url.lower().startswith("http"):
            self.url = url
            return
    
        # Support for unicode domain names and paths.
        try:
            scheme, auth, host, port, path, query, fragment = parse_url(url)
        except LocationParseError as e:
            raise InvalidURL(*e.args)
    
        if not scheme:
>           raise MissingSchema(
                f"Invalid URL {url!r}: No scheme supplied. "
                f"Perhaps you meant https://{url}?"
            )
E           requests.exceptions.MissingSchema: Invalid URL '/api/auth/login': No scheme supplied. Perhaps you meant https:///api/auth/login?

self = <PreparedRequest [POST]>, url = '/api/auth/login', params = OrderedDict()

    def prepare_url(self, url, params):
        """Prepares the given HTTP URL."""
        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238
        if isinstance(url, bytes):
            url = url.decode("utf8")
        else:
            url = str(url)
    
        # Remove leading whitespaces from url
        url = url.lstrip()
    
        # Don't do any URL preparation for non-HTTP schemes like `mailto`,
        # `data` etc to work around exceptions from `url_parse`, which
        # handles RFC 3986 only.
        if ":" in url and not url.lower().startswith("http"):
            self.url = url
            return
    
        # Support for unicode domain names and paths.
        try:
            scheme, auth, host, port, path, query, fragment = parse_url(url)
        except LocationParseError as e:
            raise InvalidURL(*e.args)
    
        if not scheme:
>           raise MissingSchema(
                f"Invalid URL {url!r}: No scheme supplied. "
                f"Perhaps you meant https://{url}?"
            )

self = <PreparedRequest [POST]>, url = '/api/auth/login', params = OrderedDict()

    def prepare_url(self, url, params):
        """Prepares the given HTTP URL."""
        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238
        if isinstance(url, bytes):
            url = url.decode("utf8")
        else:
            url = str(url)
    
        # Remove leading whitespaces from url
        url = url.lstrip()
    
        # Don't do any URL preparation for non-HTTP schemes like `mailto`,
        # `data` etc to work around exceptions from `url_parse`, which
        # handles RFC 3986 only.
        if ":" in url and not url.lower().startswith("http"):
            self.url = url
            return
    
        # Support for unicode domain names and paths.
        try:
            scheme, auth, host, port, path, query, fragment = parse_url(url)
        except LocationParseError as e:
            raise InvalidURL(*e.args)
    
        if not scheme:
>           raise MissingSchema(
                f"Invalid URL {url!r}: No scheme supplied. "
                f"Perhaps you meant https://{url}?"
            )
E           requests.exceptions.MissingSchema: Invalid URL '/api/auth/login': No scheme supplied. Perhaps you meant https:///api/auth/login?

self = <PreparedRequest [POST]>, url = '/api/auth/login', params = OrderedDict()

    def prepare_url(self, url, params):
        """Prepares the given HTTP URL."""
        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238
        if isinstance(url, bytes):
            url = url.decode("utf8")
        else:
            url = str(url)
    
        # Remove leading whitespaces from url
        url = url.lstrip()
    
        # Don't do any URL preparation for non-HTTP schemes like `mailto`,
        # `data` etc to work around exceptions from `url_parse`, which
        # handles RFC 3986 only.
        if ":" in url and not url.lower().startswith("http"):
            self.url = url
            return
    
        # Support for unicode domain names and paths.
        try:
            scheme, auth, host, port, path, query, fragment = parse_url(url)
        except LocationParseError as e:
            raise InvalidURL(*e.args)
    
        if not scheme:
>           raise MissingSchema(
                f"Invalid URL {url!r}: No scheme supplied. "
                f"Perhaps you meant https://{url}?"
            )
E           requests.exceptions.MissingSchema: Invalid URL '/api/auth/login': No scheme supplied. Perhaps you meant https:///api/auth/login?

self = <PreparedRequest [POST]>, url = '/api/auth/login', params = OrderedDict()

    def prepare_url(self, url, params):
        """Prepares the given HTTP URL."""
        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238
        if isinstance(url, bytes):
            url = url.decode("utf8")
        else:
            url = str(url)
    
        # Remove leading whitespaces from url
        url = url.lstrip()
    
        # Don't do any URL preparation for non-HTTP schemes like `mailto`,
        # `data` etc to work around exceptions from `url_parse`, which
        # handles RFC 3986 only.
        if ":" in url and not url.lower().startswith("http"):
            self.url = url
            return
    
        # Support for unicode domain names and paths.
        try:
            scheme, auth, host, port, path, query, fragment = parse_url(url)
        except LocationParseError as e:
            raise InvalidURL(*e.args)
    
        if not scheme:
>           raise MissingSchema(
                f"Invalid URL {url!r}: No scheme supplied. "
                f"Perhaps you meant https://{url}?"
            )

    def test_scope3_3_maps_to_scope3_amont(self):

        """

self = <PreparedRequest [GET]>, url = '/api/categories', params = OrderedDict()

    def prepare_url(self, url, params):
        """Prepares the given HTTP URL."""
        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238
        if isinstance(url, bytes):
            url = url.decode("utf8")
        else:
            url = str(url)
    
        # Remove leading whitespaces from url
        url = url.lstrip()
    
        # Don't do any URL preparation for non-HTTP schemes like `mailto`,
        # `data` etc to work around exceptions from `url_parse`, which
        # handles RFC 3986 only.
        if ":" in url and not url.lower().startswith("http"):
            self.url = url
            return
    
        # Support for unicode domain names and paths.
        try:
            scheme, auth, host, port, path, query, fragment = parse_url(url)
        except LocationParseError as e:
            raise InvalidURL(*e.args)
    
        if not scheme:
>           raise MissingSchema(
                f"Invalid URL {url!r}: No scheme supplied. "
                f"Perhaps you meant https://{url}?"
            )
E           requests.exceptions.MissingSchema: Invalid URL '/api/categories': No scheme supplied. Perhaps you meant https:///api/categories?

_ TestGHGProtocolRulesWithSpecificFactors.test_scope1_entry_chaudiere_mazout_creates_scope1_and_scope3_3 _

self = <test_ghg_protocol_rules.TestGHGProtocolRulesWithSpecificFactors object at 0xf9e2249c9510>

    def test_scope1_entry_chaudiere_mazout_creates_scope1_and_scope3_3(self):
        """
        Test: Scope 1 entry (combustion_fixe) with Chaudière mazout
        Expected: Creates scope1 (cat=combustion_fixe) + scope3_3 (cat=activites_combustibles_energie)
    
        Business Rule: Scope 1 entry → include scope1, scope2, scope3_3 impacts
        """
        activity_data = {
            "category_id": "combustion_fixe",
            "subcategory_id": "combustibles",
            "scope": "scope1",
            "name": "TEST_GHG_Scope1_Chaudiere",
            "quantity": 100,
            "unit": "MJ",
            "emission_factor_id": CHAUDIERE_MAZOUT_ID,
            "entry_scope": "scope1",
            "entry_category": "combustion_fixe"
        }
    
        response = requests.post(
            f"{BASE_URL}/api/activities",
            headers=self.headers,
            json=activity_data
        )
    
        assert response.status_code == 200, f"Failed to create activity: {response.text}"
        result = response.json()
    
        # Should return a group with 2 activities (scope1 + scope3_3)
        # scope3 is excluded because it's not in [scope1, scope2, scope3_3] for Scope 1 entry
        assert "group_id" in result, "Expected multi-activity response for Scope 1 entry"
    
        activities = result.get("activities", [])
>       assert len(activities) == 2, f"Expected 2 activities for Scope 1 entry, got {len(activities)}"
E       AssertionError: Expected 2 activities for Scope 1 entry, got 0
E       assert 0 == 2
E        +  where 0 = len([])

            "name": "TEST_Scope3_3_Hydro_Entry",
            "quantity": 1000,
            "unit": "kWh",
            "emission_factor_id": HYDRO_FACTOR_ID,
            "entry_scope": "scope3_amont",
            "entry_category": "activites_combustibles_energie"  # This triggers scope3_3 rule
        }

            headers=self.headers,
            json=activity_data
        )
    
        assert response.status_code == 200, f"Failed to create activity: {response.text}"
        result = response.json()
    
        # When only 1 activity is created, API returns single activity object (not wrapped in group)
        # Check if it's a single activity response (has 'id' but no 'activities' array)
        if "activities" in result:
            # Multi-activity response
            activities = result.get("activities", [])
            assert len(activities) == 1, f"Expected 1 activity for Scope 3.3 entry, got {len(activities)}"
            assert activities[0]["scope"] == "scope3_3", f"Expected scope3_3, got {activities[0]['scope']}"
    
            # Verify emissions
            expected_emissions = 1000 * 0.00388983
            assert abs(activities[0]["emissions"] - expected_emissions) < 0.001
    
            # Cleanup
            group_id = result["group_id"]
            requests.delete(f"{BASE_URL}/api/activities/groups/{group_id}", headers=self.headers)
        else:
            # Single activity response (when only 1 impact applies)

params = OrderedDict()

    def prepare_url(self, url, params):
        """Prepares the given HTTP URL."""
        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238
        if isinstance(url, bytes):
            url = url.decode("utf8")
        else:
            url = str(url)
    
        # Remove leading whitespaces from url
        url = url.lstrip()
    
        # Don't do any URL preparation for non-HTTP schemes like `mailto`,
        # `data` etc to work around exceptions from `url_parse`, which
        # handles RFC 3986 only.
        if ":" in url and not url.lower().startswith("http"):
            self.url = url
            return
    
        # Support for unicode domain names and paths.
        try:
            scheme, auth, host, port, path, query, fragment = parse_url(url)
        except LocationParseError as e:
            raise InvalidURL(*e.args)
    
        if not scheme:
>           raise MissingSchema(
                f"Invalid URL {url!r}: No scheme supplied. "
                f"Perhaps you meant https://{url}?"
            )
E           requests.exceptions.MissingSchema: Invalid URL '/api/auth/onboarding/reset': No scheme supplied. Perhaps you meant https:///api/auth/onboarding/reset?

    def test_record_product_sale_enhanced(self, auth_token):
        """Test recording a sale and verifying Scope 3 Aval activities are created"""
        # First get an enhanced product
        products_res = requests.get(
            f"{BASE_URL}/api/products",
            headers={"Authorization": f"Bearer {auth_token}"}
        )
        products = products_res.json()
        enhanced_products = [p for p in products if p.get("is_enhanced")]
    
        if not enhanced_products:
            pytest.skip("No enhanced products available for sale test")
    
        product = enhanced_products[0]
        product_id = product["id"]
    
        # Record a sale
        sale_data = {
            "product_id": product_id,
            "quantity": 10,
            "year": 2025
        }
    
        response = requests.post(
            f"{BASE_URL}/api/products/{product_id}/sales/enhanced",
            headers={"Authorization": f"Bearer {auth_token}"},
            json=sale_data
        )

self = <PreparedRequest [GET]>, url = '/api/units/dimensions'
params = OrderedDict()

    def prepare_url(self, url, params):
        """Prepares the given HTTP URL."""
        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238
        if isinstance(url, bytes):
            url = url.decode("utf8")
        else:
            url = str(url)
    
        # Remove leading whitespaces from url
        url = url.lstrip()
    
        # Don't do any URL preparation for non-HTTP schemes like `mailto`,
        # `data` etc to work around exceptions from `url_parse`, which
        # handles RFC 3986 only.
        if ":" in url and not url.lower().startswith("http"):
            self.url = url
            return
    
        # Support for unicode domain names and paths.
        try:
            scheme, auth, host, port, path, query, fragment = parse_url(url)
        except LocationParseError as e:
            raise InvalidURL(*e.args)
    
        if not scheme:
>           raise MissingSchema(
                f"Invalid URL {url!r}: No scheme supplied. "
                f"Perhaps you meant https://{url}?"
            )
E           requests.exceptions.MissingSchema: Invalid URL '/api/units/dimensions': No scheme supplied. Perhaps you meant https:///api/units/dimensions?
